### Error Diagnosis

1.  **Error in `log.blockMesh`: "Block hex ... has inward-pointing faces"**
    *   **Cause:** The `blockMeshDict` file defines the vertices and blocks for the geometry. The error indicates that the vertex ordering for the hexahedral block `hex (0 1 2 3 4 5 6 7)` is incorrect. In OpenFOAM, the vertices of a hexahedron must be ordered such that the faces point outward from the block. The current ordering `(0 1 2 3 4 5 6 7)` creates a self-intersecting or inverted volume for the specific vertex coordinates provided in the file.
    *   **Context:** The vertices are defined in a specific order, but the block definition does not correctly traverse them to form a valid mesh volume. The vertices `0` to `3` form the "front" face, and `4` to `7` form the "back" face. The current ordering likely swaps the front/back or side connections, causing the mesh to fold in on itself.

2.  **Error in `log.rhoSimpleFoam`: "Cannot find file 'points' in directory 'polyMesh'"**
    *   **Cause:** This is a direct consequence of the first error. Because `blockMesh` failed to generate the mesh (due to the inverted block), the `polyMesh` directory was never created or populated with the necessary files (`points`, `faces`, `cells`). Consequently, when `rhoSimpleFoam` attempts to start, it cannot find the mesh data required to begin the simulation.
    *   **Resolution:** Fixing the `blockMeshDict` geometry will allow `blockMesh` to run successfully, creating the `polyMesh` directory and the `points` file, which will resolve the second error.

    *   **Cause:** The vertex ordering in the `blocks` section of `system/blockMeshDict` is incorrect for the specific coordinates provided. In OpenFOAM, the vertices of a hexahedron must be ordered such that the faces point outward. The current ordering `hex (0 1 2 3 4 5 6 7)` (and similar for other blocks) creates a twisted or inverted volume because the winding order of the second face (vertices 4-7) is inconsistent with the first face (vertices 0-3) relative to the block's interior.
    *   **Specific Issue:** The error message explicitly points to faces like `4(0 4 8 12)` being inward. This indicates that the connection between the "start" face and the "end" face of the hexahedron is reversed.

2.  **`log.rhoSimpleFoam`: "Cannot find file 'points' in directory 'polyMesh'"**
    *   **Cause:** This is a direct consequence of the `blockMesh` failure. Since the mesh generation failed, the `polyMesh` directory was not created, and consequently, the `points` file (and others) are missing. The solver cannot start without a valid mesh.

3.  **Field Definition Mismatches (Critical)**
    *   **Cause:** The provided `foamfiles` list for the `0` directory contains severe mismatches between the file name, the `object` name, and the `class` type.
        *   File `p` has `object U` and `class volVectorField`.
        *   File `U` has `object T` and `class volScalarField`.
        *   File `T` has `object U` and `class volVectorField`.
    *   **Impact:** Even if the mesh is fixed, `rhoSimpleFoam` will fail immediately because it expects `p` (pressure) to be a scalar field and `U` (velocity) to be a vector field. The solver will look for `p` (scalar) but find a vector field named `U`, or fail to find `p` entirely if the object name is `U`.

### Proposed Solutions

**1. Fix `blockMeshDict` Vertex Ordering**
The primary geometric error must be resolved to generate the mesh. The vertex ordering for the hexahedral blocks needs to be corrected to ensure outward-pointing faces.

    *   **Change:** `hex (0 1 2 3 4 5 6 7)` -> **`hex (0 1 2 3 7 6 5 4)`**
    *   **Change:** `hex (0 1 13 12 4 5 9 8)` -> **`hex (0 1 13 12 8 9 5 4)`**
    *   **Change:** `hex (1 3 15 13 5 7 11 9)` -> **`hex (1 3 15 13 9 11 7 5)`**
    *   **Change:** `hex (0 2 14 12 4 6 10 8)` -> **`hex (0 2 14 12 8 10 6 4)`**
    *   **Change:** `hex (2 3 15 14 6 7 11 10)` -> **`hex (2 3 15 14 10 11 7 6)`**
    *   **Change:** `hex (8 9 15 14 10 11 13 12)` -> **`hex (8 9 15 14 12 13 11 10)`**
    *   *Note:* This reversal corrects the winding order for the second face, ensuring the volume is defined correctly without inward-pointing faces.

**2. Correct Field Definitions in `0` Directory**
The field files must match the expected variable types and names for `rhoSimpleFoam`.

        *   Ensure `dimensions` are `[0 0 0 1 0 0 0]`.
        *   Ensure `boundaryField` for `inlet` is `fixedValue uniform 1000`.

*   **Action:** Ensure the `divSchemes` in `system/fvSchemes` are appropriate for `rhoSimpleFoam`.
*   **Specific Change:** The current `divSchemes` includes `div((nuEff*dev2(T(grad(U)))))`. While this term is often used in incompressible solvers, `rhoSimpleFoam` typically uses `div(phi, U)` for the momentum equation. The term `dev2(T(grad(U)))` is a specific tensor operation. If the solver complains about undefined keywords, ensure the term is correctly defined or removed if not needed for the specific turbulence model. However, the primary error is the mesh.

The error `Block hex ... has inward-pointing faces` persists because the vertex indices in the `blocks` section do not correctly traverse the vertices to form a valid volume for the specific coordinates provided. The standard "reversal" strategy failed because the vertex indices (0-15) are not laid out in a simple linear order relative to the blocks.

The current `vertices` list (0-15) defines the corners. The `blocks` section must be re-defined to correctly link these corners. The most robust way to fix a "square bend" with these specific vertices is to ensure the block faces are defined by the correct sequence of vertices that form the physical faces of the bend.
